<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

In the proposed design, a reader module using a hybrid assemble technique is directly integrated inside the antenna. In order to compensate the degraded radiation efficiency of the reader antenna due to the module integration, a quadruple inverted-f antenna (QIFA), a type of four-port antenna like QIFA, is used. For the compact four-port antenna, we analyze the optimum matching method considering both the reflection coefficient at each port and the mutual coupling among ports simultaneously to improve the performance of the proposed module integrated antenna. Experimental results show that the proposed module integrated antenna of size 80 Ã 80 Ã 11.2 mm<sup>3</sup> with the shielded module is well matched, and has the peak gain of 3.3 dBic and the axial ratio under 2.5 dB.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF identification (RFID) has become a mainstream and its various applications can be found in many industries ranging from defense to healthcare, from customer to enterprise, and from supply chain to value chain <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. The RFID system is standardized in various frequency bands (low-frequency (LF), high-frequency (HF), ultrahigh-frequency (UHF), microwave RFID systems). A passive UHF RFID is standardized in 900 MHz and actively applied in distribution or regulation industries (supply chain, warehouse, or retail store management) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. The passive UHF RFID system can also be classified into portable and fixed type, depending on the range of reader usage. Recently, according to the stream of market about applying the RFID system into the mobile environment, many studies on a passive mobile UHF RFID reader are actively ongoing.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(a)</a> shows the generally used reader structure consisting of a reader module and an antenna for the portable passive UHF RFID system. The reader module is usually composed of hybrid circuits or CMOS integrated circuits (ICs) and internally has
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 1. </b><fig><p>(a) Block diagram of mobile UHF RFID reader structure (b) reader structure with reader module composed of hybrid circuits and proposed module integrated antenna with (c) square-shaped reader module (d) rectangular-shaped reader module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
RF, baseband, and digital parts <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. The reader antenna is generally implemented with circular polarization antennas such as a ceramic, microstrip patch, or spiral antenna <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, but linear polarization antennas like dipole or inverted-f <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_1">[11]</a> can also be used.<p></p><p>As the RFID system is recently adopted into compact mobile devices like a personal digital assistant (PDA), the need for a miniaturized portable passive UHF RFID is emphasized. Thus, various research to reduce the size of the reader are ongoing, but the studies are restricted to miniaturize the reader antenna and the reader modules individually.</p><p>Therefore, the module integrated antenna for a portable UHF RFID is proposed to reduce the size of the whole reader system. In the proposed module integrated antenna, the reader module is directly integrated inside the antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(c) and (d)</a>. Also, a four-port antenna, quadruple inverted-f antenna (QIFA), is used instead of the generally used one-port antenna in order to improve the reduced radiation efficiency of the reader antenna due to the module integration. For the compact QIFA, we analyze the optimum matching method considering both the reflection coefficient at each port and the mutual coupling between ports simultaneously to improve the performance of the proposed module integrated antenna.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Structure of Module Integrated Antenna</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. QIFA for Module Integrated Antenna</h3><p>Although the reader antenna with an empty space inside is required for a reader module to be internally integrated, previously used reader antennas are not applicable since they are planar types or filled with dielectric materials inside. Thus, the QIFA, a type of four-port antenna, with an empty space inside, is used as a reader antenna to integrate the module inside, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 1(c) and (d)</a>. The proposed module integrated antenna size is identical with the size of the QIFA, which consists of four inverted-f antennas. The square or rectangular-shaped shielded reader module is integrated onto the empty space inside the antenna. For a wide range of a right-hand circular polarization (RHCP) signal, four inverted-f antennas are located on each corner of the square with equal amplitude and quadrature phases (0Â°, 90Â°, 180Â°, and 270Â°). The input impedance and resonance frequency of the module integrated antenna can also be controlled by adjusting the length of the antenna and shorted matching stub.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. Feed Network for Module Integrated Antenna</h3><p>The module integrated antenna is fed by equal amplitudes, but with relative quadrature phase differences. This type of phase distribution is obtained by using a compact microstrip feed network consisting of a Wilkinson power divider, 90Â° delay line, and two 180Â° delay lines, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>. The designed feed schematic provides good RHCP gain for the module integrated antenna. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>, if the loads with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; top: -7.865em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="min-width: 10.153em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; The feed network is implemented with an FR-4 printed circuit board, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(b)</a>. The feed network is designed with a microstrip line along the edges of the circuit board in order to integrate the shielded module in the center. The feed network is also implemented on both top and bottom layers. A Wilkinson power divider and 90Â° delay line are designed on the top layer, while two 180Â° delay lines are realized on both the top and bottom layers. Ideally, the feed network generates four equal amplitude signals of â6 dB with phase differences of 0Â°, 90Â°, 180Â°, and 270Â°, but the fabricated feed network have insertion loss of about 0.7â0.9 dB and phase error of about <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-148" role="math" style="width: 2.225em; <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Design of the Module Integrated Antenna</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Matching Condition of Module Integrated Antenna (Square-Shaped Module)</h3><p>In order to integrate the reader module into the inside of the reader antenna, the QIFA, four-port antenna, is used. However, when the size of the four-port antenna like QIFA is reduced for mobile applications, the mutual coupling among each port occurs and antenna matching gets worse. Moreover, as the reader module is integrated inside the antenna, the antenna performance gets degraded. Therefore, we propose and analyze a new matching method considering both the mutual coupling for the compact four-port antenna and the effect of the internally integrated reader module in order to improve the performance of the compact module integrated antenna. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 4</a> shows the equivalent-circuit model of the module integrated antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 4. </b><fig><p>Equivalent-circuit model of the proposed module integrated antenna with square-shaped module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>Having the reflection and mutual coupling of the four-port antenna considered in the equivalent circuit, the reflection coefficient at port <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-13-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-167" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; Matching Condition of Module Integrated Antenna (Rectangular-Shaped Module)</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 5. </b><fig><p>Equivalent-circuit model of the proposed module integrated antenna with rectangular-shaped module.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> shows the equivalent-circuit model of the rectangular-shaped module integrated antenna. Compared to the case that the square-shaped module is integrated inside the antenna, the relations of the reflection coefficients and mutual coupling coefficients in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn11" href="#deqn11" class="fulltext-link">(11)</a> are no longer valid for the rectangular-shaped module integrated antenna. That is, the couplings between each antenna and the rectangular-shaped module are not the same, although the distances between the adjacent ports are consistent. The couplings from the antennas at ports 4â6, and the rectangular module are the same, but different from the couplings from the antennas at ports 5â7, and the rectangular module. The relations of the reflection coefficients and the mutual coupling coefficients for the rectangular-shaped module integrated antenna are represented as follows: <disp-formula id="deqn13" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-35-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1121" role="math" style="width: 100%; Thus far, the optimum matching method to improve the degraded matching due to the rectangular- or square-shaped module integration has been theoretically analyzed and proposed. For the proposed module integrated antenna, QIFA is used to improve the matching by adjusting the reflection coefficients at each port and the mutual coupling coefficients among ports.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1672" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Î</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1673"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1674"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1675" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1676" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">(\Gamma_{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with the mutual coupling coefficient between ports 2 and 4 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1677" role="math" style="width: 3.847em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.426em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.31em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1678"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1679" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1680"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.646em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1681" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1682"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1683"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1684" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">f<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1685" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1686" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1687" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">42</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1688" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">(M_{\rm far42})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6(b)</a> show the difference of about 16 dB and 105Â°, respectively, thus, the first and second conditions of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14" href="#deqn14" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> are not satisfied. The simulated radiation efficiency in this case is about 38%, which implies that the matching is not efficiently done. In order to satisfy <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14" href="#deqn14" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a>, the vertical and horizontal lengths of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1689" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1690"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1691" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the short stub for the inverted-f antennas at ports 1 and 3 and the inverted-f antennas at ports 2 and 4 are independently adjusted, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10(a)</a>. That is, the horizontal and vertical lengths of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1692" role="math" style="width: 0.724em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.664em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1693"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1694" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">L</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the short stub for the inverted-f antennas at ports 1 and 3 are set to 53, 6, and 8 mm, while the ones at ports 2 and 4 are set to 47, 7, and 3 mm, respectively. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10(b)â(d)</a>, <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14" href="#deqn14" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> is satisfied at the center frequency and the matching is well performed since the radiation efficiency is improved to about 75% comparing to the radiation efficiency of 38% in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. Since the proposed module integrated antenna uses a four-port antenna instead of a one-port antenna as a reader antenna, each port can be independently adjusted to optimize the antenna characteristic. Therefore, the antenna matching can be efficiently performed although an asymmetric rectangular-shaped module is integrated inside.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 11</a> shows the overall structure of the proposed module integrated antenna. The proposed antenna has the width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1695" role="math" style="width: 2.405em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.165em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.04em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1696"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1697" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1698"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1699" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">W<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1700"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1701"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1702" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1703" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">(W_{a})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 80 mm and the height of 11.2 mm. The horizontal and vertical part of the inverted-f antennas are all fabricated with FR-4 board (thickness: 0.6 mm, relative permittivity: 4.8).</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Measurement Results</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12</a> shows the implemented module integrated antenna for the UHF RFID reader. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12(a)</a>, we can know that the implemented module is integrated on the implemented feed network and the module integrated antenna with a shielded module is implemented as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 12(d)</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 13</a> shows the measured return loss of the proposed module integrated antenna. The module integrated antenna resonates well at the center frequency and has the reflection characteristic of less than â10 dB in the bandwidth of about 200 MHz.

<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 14. </b><fig><p>Measured peak gain of the proposed module integrated antenna when the matching is not performed (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>) and performed well (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>) in frequency range from 900 to 930 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 15. </b><fig><p>Measured axial ratio of the proposed module integrated antenna optimized in frequency range from 900 to 930 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The peak gain and axial ratio of the proposed module integrated antenna are also measured from 900 to 930 MHz in the authorized anechoic chamber using a network analyzer and reference horn antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 14</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">15</a>. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3d" class="fulltext-link">SectionÂ III-D</a>, we shows that the module integrated antenna with the rectangular-shaped module, which is matched well (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a>), has the improved radiation efficiency of about 75% compared to the poorly matched case (<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>) of about 38%. Thus, we experimentally compare the performance of both cases of implemented antennas by measuring the peak gain. As shown in
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 16. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation pattern of the proposed module integrated antenna at the center frequency of 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5745706/5728890/5728890-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 17. </b><fig><p>Measured radiation pattern of the proposed module integrated antenna at the center frequency of 915 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5728890/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 14</a>, the peak gain at the center frequency is 3.3 dBic when the matching is performed well, but when the matching is not performed, the measured peak gain at the center frequency is 1.6 dBic. Thus, we can know that proposed module integrated antenna has improved performance when the optimum matching condition is applied. The axial ratio is also measured less than about 2.5 dB, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>, and 3-dB gain and axial ratio bandwidth is measured less than 100 MHz, but the bandwidth of the peak gain and axial ratio is narrower than the bandwidth of the return loss because of the narrow bandwidth of the 90Â° and 180Â° delay lines in the feed network, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2(a)</a>. Although the bandwidth of the peak gain and axial ratio is narrower than the bandwidth of the return loss, it can sufficiently be used in the U.S. passive UHF RFID band. The proposed module integrated antenna has the directivity in zenith direction and the 3-dB beamwidth of about 130Â°.<p></p><p>To validate the performance of the proposed module integrated antenna in UHF RFID reader applications, the reading-range measurement was also carried out using a proposed module integrated antenna to detect a UHF RFID tag in the authorized anechoic chamber, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(a)</a>. We especially measured the reading range by rotating a tag like a Ferris wheel to validate both the reading performance and circular polarization performance simultaneously. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(b)</a>, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2095" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; Thus, it is noted that the reading performance is good and the circular polarization performance is also good, as mentioned above in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 15</a>, but the reading range decreased to 3.35 m and the maximum difference increased to 10 cm at 905 MHz because the peak gain and axial ratio get worse, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Figs.Â 14</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">15</a>. In addition, we carried out the reading-range measurement using two tags, which are vertically arranged, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 17(c)</a>. In this case, the reading range is measured only when two tags are detected simultaneously. The maximum reading range was measured at about 3.5 m at 915 MHz when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-2111" role="math" style="width: 7.21em; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2115"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2116"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2117" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2118" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">X</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-2119" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-2120" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">30</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-2121" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2122"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2123"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-2124"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2125"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-2126" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">P_{\rm TX}=30\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, but the maximum difference increased to 10 cm compared to the measured result using single tag. At 905 MHz, the reading range decreased to 3.35 m, and the maximum difference increased to 15 cm.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A module integrated antenna with circular polarization for a mobile UHF RFID reader has been presented and measured. In order to compensate the degraded performance of the module integrated antenna by integrating the reader module, we analyzed the optimum matching method in case of integrating not only the square-shaped module, but also the rectangular-shaped module. Based on the proposed matching method, the module integrated antenna has been optimized to have high efficiency. Excellent matching and optimal performance of the fabricated module integrated antenna have been verified experimentally as well. The optimized module integrated antenna had a peak gain of about 3.3 dBic, an axial ratio of less than 2.5 dB, and a 3-dB beamwidth of more than 130Â°.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

</script>
